# Data Flow Q&A: Envoy Request Routing

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/envoy--d7809ba2 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/envoy--d7809ba2 (mirror of envoyproxy/envoy)
**Task Type:** Data Flow Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Envoy is a high-performance proxy that routes HTTP requests from downstream clients to upstream services. Understanding the complete path from the initial TCP accept through filter processing to the final upstream connection is critical for working with Envoy's architecture.

## Task

Trace the complete path of a single HTTP request from the moment a downstream client TCP connection is accepted through filter chain processing, route resolution, upstream cluster selection, and connection establishment. Identify every key transformation point, component boundary crossing, and state change.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Envoy's request routing flow:

### Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain

When a downstream client establishes a TCP connection to Envoy, how does the request travel from socket accept to network filter processing?

- Which component accepts the incoming TCP connection?
- How does Envoy select which network filter chain to apply based on connection properties?
- At what point does the connection get handed to the HTTP Connection Manager (HCM)?
- What triggers the initial `onData()` call when bytes arrive?

### Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration

Once bytes arrive at the HCM, how does Envoy parse HTTP and iterate through filters?

- How does the codec parse the byte stream into HTTP headers/body?
- When is the `ActiveStream` created and how does it relate to filter iteration?
- How does the `FilterManager` determine the order of decoder filter execution?
- What filter return values can stop or continue iteration?

### Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection

When the router filter is invoked, how does it select the upstream destination?

- How does the router determine which route configuration to use?
- What is the sequence of operations that resolves a route entry to a specific upstream cluster?
- How does the router select a specific upstream host from the cluster?
- What triggers the creation of the upstream connection?

### Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow

Once an upstream host is selected, how does Envoy establish the connection and forward the request?

- How does the connection pool provide or create an upstream connection?
- What component actually writes the HTTP request to the upstream socket?
- How does the response flow back from upstream through the filter chain?
- At what points does the encoder filter chain get invoked vs. the decoder filter chain?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:

```
# Envoy Request Routing Flow

## Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Evidence
<consolidated list of supporting file paths and line references>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Cite specific files, classes, and methods — avoid vague or speculative answers
- Focus on the core request path, not error handling or edge cases
- Trace a single successful HTTP/1.1 request without TLS termination

72-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of Envoy's request routing flow. Here's a summary of what I've documented:

## Complete Data Flow Traced

I've written a detailed investigation document (`/logs/agent/investigation.md`) that traces an HTTP request through all four phases:

### **Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain**
- Socket accept in `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()`
- Listener filter chain processing with `ActiveTcpSocket`
- Network filter chain selection based on matching criteria
- Hand-off to HTTP Connection Manager via `onNewConnection()` and `onData()`

### **Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration**
- Codec creation and dispatch in `ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()`
- `ActiveStream` instantiation via `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()`
- HTTP filter chain iteration with `ActiveStreamDecoderFilter` wrappers
- Filter state management (Continue/StopIteration controls)

### **Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection**
- Route matching via `callbacks_->route()` 
- Cluster resolution from route entry
- Host selection via `cluster->chooseHost()` with load balancing
- Connection pool acquisition with `createConnPool()`

### **Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow**
- `UpstreamRequest` creation with `GenericConnPool`
- Connection request via `conn_pool_->newStream(this)`
- Request encoding through `UpstreamCodecFilter` to upstream socket
- Response reception through `CodecBridge` back through filter chains
- Encoder chain processing and downstream response delivery

The document includes **specific file paths and line numbers** throughout, making each component easily traceable in the actual codebase.

`source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.cc:TcpListenerImpl::onAccept()` - libevent-based socket accept\n   - Socket is wrapped and passed to `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()`\n\n2. **ActiveTcpListener Processing** (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc`)\n   - `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept(Network::ConnectionSocketPtr&& socket)` (line 80)\n   - Checks connection limits via `listenerConnectionLimitReached()`\n   - Calls `onAcceptWorker()` which handles connection balancing across worker threads\n   - Creates `ActiveTcpSocket` (line 126)\n\n3. **Listener Filter Chain** (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc`)\n   - `ActiveTcpSocket` constructor (line 11) initializes the accepted socket\n   - Listener filters are processed in `continueFilterChain()` (line 111)\n   - Each listener filter's `onAccept()` is called; filters can pause and request more data\n   - `createListenerFilterBuffer()` (line 73) manages buffered data for listener filters\n\n4. **Network Filter Chain Selection** (`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc`)\n   - After listener filters complete, socket transitions to `ActiveTcpConnection`\n   - Filter chain is selected based on the `FilterChain::matchTransportSocket()` matching\n   - The matching criteria (e.g., TLS SNI, source IP) determine which filter chain to use\n   - Network filter factory creates the HTTP Connection Manager (HCM)\n\n5. **Hand-off to Network Filter Manager**\n   - `OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase::onSocketAccepted()` processes the filter chain\n   - For HTTP, the HTTP Connection Manager is instantiated as a Network::Filter\n   - The established TCP connection calls the HCM's `onNewConnection()` method\n   - HCM initializes and prepares to receive data\n\n### Data Arrival and HCM Invocation\n\n6. **onData() Triggering**\n   - Socket receives bytes \u2192 dispatcher triggers `onData()` callback\n   - `ConnectionManagerImpl::onData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool)` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:486)\n   - HCM creates codec lazily on first `onData()` call (line 488-496)\n\n## Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration\n\n### Codec Creation and Header Parsing\n\n1. **Codec Instantiation** (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`)\n   - `ConnectionManagerImpl::createCodec(Buffer::Instance& data)` creates HTTP codec\n   - Codec type (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, HTTP/3) determined from data\n   - Supports load shedding via `hcm_ondata_creating_codec_` overload point\n\n2. **Codec Dispatch** (line 503)\n   - `codec_->dispatch(data)` parses incoming bytes\n   - Codec invokes `ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()` when headers are complete\n   - Returns HTTP status; errors trigger immediate connection closure\n\n### ActiveStream Creation\n\n3. **Stream Instantiation** (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:387`)\n   - `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream(ResponseEncoder& response_encoder, bool is_internally_created)`\n   - Creates new `ActiveStream` - wraps a single HTTP request/response pair\n   - Initializes stream with `buffer_limit` and accounting information\n   - Returns `RequestDecoder` interface for codec to deliver parsed data\n\n4. **Stream Structure** (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h:141`)\n   - `ActiveStream` is `LinkedObject<ActiveStream>` - maintains list of concurrent streams\n   - 1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Envoy Request Routing Flow

This document traces the complete path of an HTTP request from TCP accept through upstream connection establishment.

## Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain

### TCP Connection Accept

When a downstream client TCP connection arrives at Envoy:

1. **Socket Accept**: The TCP listener accepts the socket in the event loop
   - `source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.cc:TcpListenerImpl::onAccept()` - libevent-based socket accept
   - Socket is wrapped and passed to `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()`

2. **ActiveTcpListener Processing** (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc`)
   - `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept(Network::ConnectionSocketPtr&& socket)` (line 80)
   - Checks connection limits via `listenerConnectionLimitReached()`
   - Calls `onAcceptWorker()` which handles connection balancing across worker threads
   - Creates `ActiveTcpSocket` (line 126)

3. **Listener Filter Chain** (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc`)
   - `ActiveTcpSocket` constructor (line 11) initializes the accepted socket
   - Listener filters are processed in `continueFilterChain()` (line 111)
   - Each listener filter's `onAccept()` is called; filters can pause and request more data
   - `createListenerFilterBuffer()` (line 73) manages buffered data for listener filters

4. **Network Filter Chain Selection** (`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc`)
   - After listener filters complete, socket transitions to `ActiveTcpConnection`
   - Filter chain is selected based on the `FilterChain::matchTransportSocket()` matching
   - The matching criteria (e.g., TLS SNI, source IP) determine which filter chain to use
   - Network filter factory creates the HTTP Connection Manager (HCM)

5. **Hand-off to Network Filter
... (truncated)
